- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms

- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

# Firefox Necko Networking to NSS TLS Handshake Chain

## Your Task

Trace how Firefox initiates a TLS connection from the networking layer to the crypto layer. Find: 1. The C++ source file in `netwerk/protocol/http/` that creates an SSL transport for HTTPS connections (look for `nsHttpConnection` or `TLSFilterTransaction`). 2. The file in `netwerk/socket/` that defines the `nsSSLIOLayerHelpers` class which bridges Necko to NSS. 3. The file in `security/manager/ssl/` that implements `nsNSSIOLayer` — the NSS I/O layer integration. 4. The file in `security/nss/lib/ssl/` that performs the actual TLS handshake (`sslsecur.c` or `ssl3con.c`). Report the file path and key class/function for each hop.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo tracing domain.

## Available Resources

No local repositories are pre-checked out.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/firefox--871325b8` (mozilla-firefox/firefox)

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],
  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

## Evaluation

Your answer will be scored on:
- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

Perfect! I have successfully traced the Firefox TLS connection chain from the Necko networking layer all the way down to the NSS cryptography layer. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Firefox TLS Connection Chain

I've created a comprehensive answer file at `/workspace/answer.json` that documents the complete chain:

### **The 7-Hop Chain:**

1. **netwerk/protocol/http/nsHttpConnection** — The main HTTP connection class that initiates HTTPS connections

2. **netwerk/protocol/http/TlsHandshaker** — Orchestrates TLS setup and handshake callbacks (SetupSSL, InitSSLParams)

3. **netwerk/protocol/http/TLSTransportLayer** — Secondary TLS encryption layer that wraps socket transport

4. **security/manager/ssl/nsNSSIOLayer (nsSSLIOLayerHelpers)** — Bridges Necko to NSS by managing SSL I/O layer creation

5. **security/manager/ssl/nsSSLSocketProvider** — Socket provider that calls nsSSLIOLayerNewSocket/AddToSocket to attach SSL

6. **security/nss/lib/ssl/sslsecur.c (ssl_Do1stHandshake)** — Orchestrates the TLS handshake state machine

7. **security/nss/lib/ssl/ssl3con.c** — Implements actual TLS 1.2/1.3 protocol logic and cryptographic operations

### **Key Files Identified:**
- HTTP layer: `nsHttpConnection.h/cpp`, `TlsHandshaker.h/cpp`, `TLSTransportLayer.h/cpp`
- SSL manager: `nsNSSIOLayer.h/cpp`, `nsSSLSocketProvider.h/cpp`
- NSS crypto: `sslsecur.c`, `ssl3con.c`

The answer file includes both the chain of symbols and complete file listing with detailed descriptions of how each layer communicates with the next.

It repeatedly calls the current handshake function pointer (ss->handshake) until the handshake is complete. TlsHandshaker::SetupSSL() is called with the connection info\\n3. TlsHandshaker::InitSSLParams() configures SSL parameters via nsITLSSocketControl\\n4. nsSSLSocketProvider::NewSocket() or AddToSocket() is invoked\\n5. nsSSLIOLayerNewSocket()/AddToSocket() in nsNSSIOLayer.cpp adds SSL layer to PRFileDesc\\n6. NSS I/O layer methods forward I/O to ssl_Do1stHandshake() in sslsecur.c\\n7. ssl_Do1stHandshake() drives the state machine through handshake phases\\n8. ssl3con.c handlers process handshake messages and perform cryptographic operations\\n9. Upon completion, ssl_FinishHandshake() is called and the secure connection is ready\\n\\nThe key innovation is that Firefox's TLSTransportLayer provides an additional abstraction that can wrap existing nsSocketTransport objects, allowing HTTPS-over-HTTPS proxying and CONNECT tunnels without breaking the existing socket abstraction.\"\n}\n",

Contains state machine handlers for processing ClientHello, ServerHello, Certificate, Finished messages, and performing key derivation and encryption setup. Also contains tls13con.h handlers for TLS 1.3 specific operations.\\n\\n**Complete Call Flow:**\\n1. nsHttpConnection::Open() initiates an HTTPS connection\\n2. TlsHandshaker::SetupSSL() is called with the connection info\\n3. TlsHandshaker::InitSSLParams() configures SSL parameters via nsITLSSocketControl\\n4. nsSSLSocketProvider::NewSocket() or AddToSocket() is invoked\\n5. nsSSLIOLayerNewSocket()/AddToSocket() in nsNSSIOLayer.cpp adds SSL layer to PRFileDesc\\n6. NSS I/O layer methods forward I/O to ssl_Do1stHandshake() in sslsecur.c\\n7. ssl_Do1stHandshake() drives the state machine through handshake phases\\n8. ssl3con.c handlers process handshake messages and perform cryptographic operations\\n9. Upon completion, ssl_FinishHandshake() is called and the secure connection is ready\\n\\nThe key innovation is that Firefox's TLSTransportLayer provides an additional abstraction that can wrap existing nsSocketTransport objects, allowing HTTPS-over-HTTPS proxying and CONNECT tunnels without breaking the existing socket abstraction.\"\n}\n",
